[Bhс╣Ыgu.тАФpa├▒capa├▒c─Б┼Ыat. ─Бgneyam uta mantroktadevatyam; 21-33. m─Бrtvyaс╕е. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham; 2, 5, 12-20, 34-36, 38-41, 43, 51, 54. anuс╣гс╣нubh (16. kakummat─л par─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 18. nicс╣Ыt; 40. purast─Бtkakuvimat─л); 3. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 6. bhurig ─Бrс╣г─л pan╠Дkti; 7, 45. jagat─л; 8, 48, 49. bhurij; 9. anuс╣гс╣нubgarbh─Б vipar─лtap─Бdalakс╣гm─л pan╠Дkti; 37. purast─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 42. 3-p. 1-av. bhurig ─Бrc─л g─Бyatr─л; 44. 1-av. 2-p. ─Бrc─л bс╣Ыhat─л; 46. 1-av. 2-p. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; 47. 5-p. b─Бrhatav─Бir─Бjagarbh─Б jagat─л; 50. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdvir─Бс╕Н bс╣Ыhat─л; 52. purast─Бdvir─Бс╕Н bс╣Ыhat─л; 55. bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б.]

Comment

тМКPartly proseтАФvss. 42, 44.тМЛ Found also (except vss. 36, 52) in P─Бipp. xvii., with slight differences of order, pointed out under the verses. The whole hymn (which is also an anuv─Бka) is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 69. 7 (with vii. 62 and the mah─Б╠Б┼Ы─Бnti hymns), in the ceremony of preparing the house-fire; and a large proportion of the verses in this and other ceremonies; a few also are used in the V─Бit.; тМКand the hymn is cited by D─Бrila on K─Бu┼Ы. 43. 5тМЛ.

Translation
  1. Ascend the reeds (naс╕Н├б); no place for thee is here; this lead is
    thy portion; come! what y├бkс╣гma is in kine, [what] y├бkс╣гma in men,
    in company with that do thou go forth downward.
Notes

This and vss. 11, 54, and 55 are quoted together in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 5, when
putting fuel on the flesh-eating (kravy─Бd) fire; also, in 71. 8, vss.
1-4, 42, 43, 15, 16 (with iii. 21. 8), with quenching it. Ppp. combines
te тАШtra in a.

Griffith

This is no place to hold thee; mount the Nada: this lead is thine appointed share. Come hither. Together with Consumption in the cattle, Consumption in our men, go henee, go southward.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Out from here do we drive death, perdition, out the niggard; whoso
    hates us, him, O non-flesh-eating Agni, do thou eat; whomso we hate, him
    do we impel to thee.
Notes

The pada-text has in c, ├бdhi; and most of the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss.
├бdhy agne, in accordance with it, though one or two (Bs.E.) have
├бddhy agne, which is no various reading, but only an allowed
equivalent. The case is like those in i. 22. 1 and v. 20. 12 above; the
abbreviated reading adhy has been mistaken for adhi instead of
addhi, and then accented accordingly. Bp. accents also akravyaре░├бt.
Our text emends to addhy ├аgne akravy─Бt, but should read instead
agne, since there is no reason whatever for the accentuation addh├н.
A better reading would seem also to be kravy─Бt. Ppp. has adhy agne
kravy─Бd; but that, of course, might mean тАШkravy─Бt. Ppp. also has
simply aс╣Б for yam u in d, omits the second u, and ends with
suv─Бmaс╕е. тМКPpp. reads yakс╣гmas for dviс╣гmas in d. So the Ppp.
reading is adhy agne kravy─Бd aс╣Б yakс╣гmas taс╣Б te pra suv─Бmaс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

Death and Misfortune we expel, Malignity we drive away. O Agni, thou who eatest not the corpse, eat him who hateth us: him whom we hate we send to thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. If the flesh-eating Agni, or if the tiger-like, hath entered this
    stall (goс╣гс╣нh├б), being not at home (?), him, having made him to have
    beans for sacrificial butter, I send far forth; let him go unto the
    Agnis that have seat in the waters.
Notes

Part of the mss. (E.I.O.R.T.K.) have vy─Бghr├бs in a, and that is
perhaps the true reading, since -ghrya seems to be found nowhere else.
Ppp. reads in b anyok─Б vive┼Ыa, and in c tan m─Б-. The Anukr.
takes no notice of the redundant (t├бm intruded?) syllable in c. In
K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 6 the verse is used (with vss. 7 and 53) in making a libation
of crushed beans with mother-of-pearl (? ┼Ыukti) to the flesh-eating
fire which is to be banished. тМКThe verse contains reminiscences of 7 and
8 below.тМЛ

Griffith

If the corpse-eating Agni, or a tiger leaving his lair, hath entered this our homestead, With beans prepared in butter I expel him: far let him go to fires that lie in waters.

режрел рдпрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХреНрд░реБрджреНрдзрд╛рдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. If angry men put thee forth (pra-kс╣Ы), with fury, a man having died,
    that, O Agni, is easy to be arranged by thee; we make thee flame up
    again.
Notes

Ppp. reads kс╣Ыtv─Б for kruddh─Бs in a, mite for mс╣Ыte in b,
and ca for tat in c. The Anukr. appears to sanction the
resolution cakс╣Ы-ur in a. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 70. 6; also
in V─Бit. 5. 13, to accompany the removal of fire from the householder’s
to the other two fires.

Griffith

When, angered that a man hath died, we in our wrath have banished thee, That deed is easily set right through thee: we kindle thee again.

    Agni, the priest (brahm├бn), conductor of good; Brahmaс╣Зaspati hath set
    thee again, in order to length of life-time to a hundred autumns.

Griffith

Again have the Adityas, Rudras, Vasus, the Brahman, bringer of good things, O Agni, Again hath Brahmanaspati disposed thee for long life lasting through a hundred autumns.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

режрен рдпреЛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. If the flesh-eating Agni hath entered our house, seeing this other
    J─Бtavedas, him I take afar for the Fathers’ sacrifice; let him kindle
    the hot drink (gharm├б) in the highest station.
Notes

The verse is also RV. x. 16. 10, where is read vas for nas in a,
dev├бm for d┼лr├бm in c, and inv─Бt for indh─Бm in d. It is
used in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 6 with vs. 4 (see note to latter).

Griffith

I sweep afar, for sacrifice to Fathers, corpse-eating Agni who hath come among us, Although he saw this other, Jatavedas: in loftiest space let him inflame the caldron.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) рдЬрд┐рд╕ [рдХреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рддреН] рдорд╛рдВрд╕рднрдХреНрд╖рдХ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ [рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдкрдХ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖] рдиреЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ (рдЧреГрд╣рдореН) рдШрд░ рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрд╢ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, [рд╕реЛ] (рдЗрдордореН) рдЗрд╕ (рдЗрддрд░рдореН) рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ [рдЙрд╕рд╕реЗ рднрд┐рдиреНрди рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгреА] (рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╕рдореН) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ (рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреН) рджреЗрдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдкрд┐рддреГрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп) рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ [рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ] рдХреЗ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рддрдореН) рдЙрд╕ [рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ] рдХреЛ (рджреВрд░рдореН) рджреВрд░ (рд╣рд░рд╛рдорд┐) рднреЗрдЬрддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ рдФрд░ (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ [рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛] (рдкрд░рдореЗ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯ (рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдЬ рдореЗрдВ (рдШрд░реНрдордореН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ рдХреЛ (рдЗрдиреНрдзрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рдХрд░реЗ рееренрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЧрдг рдЪрддреБрд░ рдиреАрддрд┐рдЬреНрдЮ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╣рд╛рдп рд╕реЗ рдХреНрд░реВрд░ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд░реА рдЬрди рдХреЛ рдирд┐рдХрд╛рд▓ рджреЗрд╡реЗрдВ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд╕рддреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рджреНрдЧреБрдг рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рдлреИрд▓реЗрдВ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдкрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреА рдХреАрд░реНрддрд┐ рдмрдврд╝реЗ рееренрее рдпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХреБрдЫ рднреЗрдж рд╕реЗ рд╣реИтИТрдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж резрежредрезремредрезреж рее

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рентИТ(рдпрдГ) (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рддреНрд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдкрдХреЛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдГ (рдХреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рддреН) рдорд╛рдВрд╕рднрдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ рдХреНрд░реВрд░рдГ (рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрд╢) рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЧреГрд╣рдореН) рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдореН, (рдЗрдордореН) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН (рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреН) рдЕрд╡рд▓реЛрдХрдпрдиреН (рдЗрддрд░рдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджреН рднрд┐рдиреНрдирдореН (рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╕рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рддрдореН) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрдореН (рд╣рд░рд╛рдорд┐) рдирдпрд╛рдорд┐ (рдкрд┐рддреГрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп) рдкрд┐рддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкреВрдЬрдирд╛рдп (рд╕рдГ) рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ (рдШрд░реНрдордореН) рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдореНтИТрдирд┐рдШреж рейредрезренред (рдЗрдиреНрдзрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддреБ (рдкрд░рдореЗ) рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ (рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рее

Translation
  1. I send far forth the flesh-eating Agni; let him go, carrying evil

The verse is also RV. x. 16. 9 (and VS. xxxv. 19 тМКwith yamar─Б╠БjyamтМЛ): our
text defaces the meter of c, d by omitting ev├б after ih├б and
inserting dev├бs. тМКCf. MGS. ii. 1. 8 and p. 149.тМЛ This and the two
following verses are used in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 12 to accompany the removed fire.
тМКThe same three vss. are quoted by the comm. to 81. 33.тМЛ

Griffith

I drive corpse-eating Agni to a distance: sin-laden let him go to Yamas vassals. Here let this other, Jatavedas, carry oblation to the Deities, fore- knowing.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I, being sent, take the flesh-eating Agni, a death, making people
    fixed with the thunderbolt; I, knowing, separate (? ni-┼Ы─Бs) him from
    the householder’s fire; also in the world of the Fathers be he [their]
    portion.
Notes

Ppp. reads iс╣гitaс╣Б in a, and, in d, lokaс╣Б paramo yotu. The
sense of b is so strange that we cannot but suspect a corrupt text.
тМКRoth would read tс╣Ыс╣Еhantam, ZDMG. xlviii. 107.тМЛ In d, nearly all
the saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. (all save Bs.E.) read lok├й тАШpi, which is therefore
probably the true text. The description by the Anukr. of this fairly
regular triс╣гс╣нubh is very strange.

Griffith

I quickly sweep away corpse-eating Agni, Death, with his bolt potdepriving men of motion. From household fire, well-knowing, I divide him: so in the world of Fathers be his portion.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The flesh-eating Agni, active, praiseworthy, I send forth by the
    roads that the Fathers go; come thou not back by those that the gods go;
    be thou just there (├бtra); watch thou over the Fathers.
Notes

Ppp. reads, in c-d, m─Б devay─Бn─Бis pathibhir ─Б g─Б тАЩtr─Бi тАЩva, which
does not help the defective meter; of this the Anukr. takes no notice.

Griffith

Corpse-eating Agni, toil-worn, meet for praises, I send away bypaths used by the Fathers. Stay there; keep watch among the Fathers: come not again to us by ways whereon Gods travel.

Translation
  1. They kindle the devouring one (s├бс╣Бkasuka) in order to well-being,
    becoming cleansed, bright, purifying; he abandons evil (ripr├б), passes
    over sin; Agni, kindled, purifies with a good purifier.
Notes

Ppp. combines ene тАЩti in c. The Anukr. does not heed that the
first p─Бda is properly jagat─л. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 5 (see
note to vs. 1). тМКCaland, WZKM. viii. 368, thinks that this verse (not
xviii. 4. 41) is intended at K─Бu┼Ы. 86. 18.тМЛ тМКOver “devouring,” as
rendering of s├бс╣Бkasuka (which occurs in vss. 11-14, 19, 40), W. has
interlined ‘crushing’ in three instances.тМЛ

Griffith

They being cleansed and bright, the purifiers, kindle Sankasuka for our well-being. Impurity leaveth us and sin departeth: lighted by the good cleanser Agni cleanseth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. God Agni the devouring hath ascended the backs of the sky; being
    released out of sin, he hath released us from imprecation.
Notes

Some of our mss. (P.M.W.E.) read n├нr ├йс╣Зaso in c. Ppp. reads, here
and below, saс╣Бkusika-.

Griffith

Agni the God, the Breaker-up, hath mounted to the heights of heaven. Released from all transgression, he hath from the curse delivered us.

Translation
  1. On this devouring Agni do we wipe off evils; we have become fit for
    sacrifice, cleansed; may he prolong our life-times.
Notes

The verse is found also in ─Аp. ix. 3. 22 (following a verse resembling
our vs. 14), which reads saс╣Бkusuke тАШgn─Бu in a-b. Our mss., as
often in such cases, vary between t─Бriс╣гat and t─Бrс╣гat at the end
(Bs.E.D.R.K. have t─Бrс╣гat). The verse is quoted (with vss. 19, 40) in
K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 16 and 86. 19, to accompany the act of washing off (ity
abhyavanejayati).

Griffith

On Agni here, the Breaker-up, we wipe impurities away. Cleansed, fit for sacrifice have we become: may he prolong our lives.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thee from inexhaustible (? ├бnya) men, kine, horses, thee the
    flesh-eating one do we thrust outтАФthe fire that obstructs life.
Notes

Ludwig gets rid of the difficulty of ├бnya by taking it as any├б and
the nouns in a, b as datives. Ppp. reads aj├▒─Бn─Б for anyebhyas
tv─Б; in c it puts nis after kravy─Бdam. Some of our mss. (Bs.I.)
combine niс╣г kr- (n├нс╕е and kr- should be separated in our edition).
The Anukr. very unnecessarily scans the verse as 8 + 6: 8 + 9, while it
is easily read into a regular anuс╣гс╣нubh.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wipe ye off on the lead; wipe ye off on the reeds; and what on the
    consuming fire; likewise on the dark (r─Бm├б) ewe; headache on the
    pillow.
Notes

The rendering is very literal, and does not disguise the obscurity of
the connection. Ppp. reads for b agnis saс╣Бkusika┼Ы ca yaс╕е, which is
more manageable: ‘and on [that] which [is] the consuming fire’: i.e.
‘on the fire.’ тМКCaland, KZ. xxxiv. 457, comparing Avestan locutions,
says that agn─Бu saс╣Бkasuke ca yat is locative to agniс╕е saс╣Бkasuka┼Ы ca
yaс╕е: cf. vs. 40 and i. 30. 1.тМЛ The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 16; 86.
19, with vss. 13 and 40: see above, under vs. 13. The mss. in general,
according to their wont, read in a mс╣Ыс╕Нhvam (but Bs. mс╣Ыс╕Нhс╕Нham).
тМКFor ┼Ы─лrс╣гakti, see ref’s under i. 12. 3.тМЛ

Griffith

Translation
  1. Having settled what is foul upon the lead [and] headache upon the
    pillow, having wiped off on the black ewe, be ye cleansed, fit for
    sacrifice.

Griffith

Wipe off pollution, lay it in the lead and in the black-hued sheep, And headache in the cushion; then be cleansed and fit to sacri- fice.

Griffith

Go onward, Death, pursue thy special pathway apart from that which Gods are wont to travel. To thee I say it who hast eyes and hearest: great grow the number of these men around us!

Whitney
Translation
  1. These living ones have turned away from the dead; our invocation of
    the gods hath been auspicious (bhadr├б) today; we have gone forward
    unto dancing, unto laughter; may we, rich in heroes, address counsel.

Griffith

Divided from the dead are these, the living: now is our calling on the Gods successful. We have gone forth for dancing and for laughter: may we with brave sons speak to the assembly.

реирей рдЗрдордВ рдЬреАрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. I set this enclosure for the living; let not another of them now go
    to that goal; living a hundred numerous autumns, let them set an
    obstacle to death with a mountain.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 18. 4, and found also in VS. (xxxv. 15), TB. (iii.
7. ll┬│), TA. (vi. 10. 2), and ─Аp. (ix. 12. 4; xiv. 22. 3). RV. differs
from our text only by reading j─лvantu in c, and ant├бr (for
tir├бs) in d. VS. agrees throughout with RV.; TB. differs only by
having (like AV.) tir├бs in d (eс╣г─Б╠Бn nu in b is doubtless a
misprint, as m├бty├бm in d is a misprint for mс╣Ыty├║m: see the comm.
тМКthe Poona ed., p. 1137, corrects them bothтМЛ), and ├бrdham in b.
TA. reads m─Б╠Б n├│ тАШnu g─Бd and ├бrdham in b, and tir├бs and
dadmahe in d. ─Аp. agrees exactly with TB. the first time; but the
second time it has no nu (or тАШnu) in b, and dadhmahe in d.
тМКCf. MP. ii. 22. 24.тМЛ Ppp. gives, in c, jyok for ┼Ыatam, and
combines ┼Ыaradaс╣г pu-. In K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 17 the verse accompanies the
setting down (of a stone) in the door; in 72. 2 the last p─Бda is recited
while stepping over the stone.

Griffith

Here I erect this rampart for the living: let none of these, none other, reach this limit. May they survive a hundred lengthened autumns, and may they bury Death beneath this mountain.

реирек рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣рддрд╛рдпреБрд░реНрдЬрд░рд╕рдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Mount, choosing old age for life-time, pressing on, one after
    another, as many as ye be; you here let Tvashс╣нar, him of good births, in
    accord [with you], lead on to living your whole life-time.
Notes

The verse is (once more with exception of the last p─Бda) RV. x. 18. 6,
and found also in TA. (vi. 10. 1). RV. reads с╣гс╣нha after y├бti in
b, and ih├б for t─Б╠Бn vas in c, and its d is dirgh├бm ─Б╠Бyuс╕е
karati j─лv├бse vaс╕е. TA. differs from RV. by having gс╣Ыс╣З─Бn─Б╠Бs in a,
sur├бtnas (for saj├│с╣г─Бs) in c, and karatu in d. Ppp. puts
the verse after our 25, and combines in a-b vс╣Ыс╣З─Бn─Б тАЩnu. The verse
is used in K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 13 with vss. 21, 32, 44, 55, and others from
elsewhere.

Griffith

Live your full lives and find age delightful, all of you striving, one behind the other. May Tvashtar, maker of fair things, be gracious, and lead your whole lives on to full existence.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As days take place (bh┼л) one after another, as seasons go along
    with seasons, as an after one does not desert (h─Б) a precedingтАФso, O
    creator (dh─Б╠Бtс╣Ы), arrange their life-times.
Notes

This verse is RV. x. 18. 5, found also in TA. (vi. 10. 1). For s─Бk├бm,
at end of b, RV. reads s─Бdh├║, and TA. kс╕╖pt─Б╠Бс╕е.

Griffith

As the days follow days in close succession, as with the seasons duly come the seasons. As each successor fails not his foregoer, so constitute the lives of these, Ordainer!

Whitney
Translation
  1. The stony one flows (r─л); take ye hold together; play the hero,
    pass over, O friends; quit here them that are of evil courses; may we
    pass up unto powers (? v─Б╠Бja) that are free from disease.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 53. 8, and found also in VS. (xxxv. 10) and TA. (vi.
3. 2). RV. has ├║t tiс╣гс╣нhata for v─лr├бyadhvam in b, jah─Бma and
(for dur├йv─Бs) ├б┼Ыev─Бs in c, and ┼Ыiv─Б╠Бn vay├бm (for anam─лv─Б╠Бm) in
d. тМКVS. agrees with RV. save that it accents s├бkh─Бyaс╕е in b and
reads, for c, ├бtra jah─лm├│ тАШ┼Ыiv─Б y├й ├бsan.тМЛ TA. agrees in general
with RV., but has revat─лs тМКunaccentedтМЛ for r─лyate in a, and in
d puts ├║t tarema after abh├н v─Б╠Бj─Бn. Vss. 26 and 27 are quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 24 and 86. 27 to accompany the symbolical act of crossing over
northward; and in V─Бit. 12. 11 to accompany (at any time) the crossing
of streams.

Griffith

Gather your strength, my friends; the stream flows stony: acquit yourselves as men, and cross the river. Abandon here the powers that were malignant, and let us cross to powers exempt from sickness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Stand up, pass over, O friends; the stony river here runs (syand);
    quit ye here them that are unpropitious; may we pass up unto propitious
    pleasant powers.
Notes

This variation of vs. 26 gives part of the RV. variants to that vs. тМКFor
a discussion of the RV. verse, see notes to my Skt. Reader, p. 388.тМЛ
Ppp. makes b identical with 26 a. The use by K─Бu┼Ы. was stated in
the preceding note.

Griffith

Rise up erect, cross over, my companions: the stream is stony that flows here before us. Abandon here the powers that were ungracious, and let us cross to powers benign and friendly.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Take ye hold on that of all the gods in order to splendor, becoming
    cleansed, clear, purifying; stepping over difficult tracks, may we revel
    a hundred winters with all our heroes.
Notes

The first half-verse is identical with vi. 62. 3 a, b, save that the
latter begins with v─Бi┼Ыv─Бnar─л╠Бm. We have doubtless to supply n─Б╠Бvam
‘boat.’ But Ppp. has s┼лnс╣Ыt─Бm for varcase in a; and the comm. to
Nirukta vi. 12 quotes the prat─лka in this form, explaining s┼лnс╣Ыt─Бm
by v─Бcam (Roth). According to K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 6, it is a young heifer
(vatsatar─л) that is caused to be laid hold on.

Griffith

Becoming pure and bright and purifying begin the Vaisvadevi strain for splendour.. May we rejoice, o’erpassing troublous places, with all our heroes through a hundred winters.

Whitney
Translation
  1. By upward roads, full of wind, by distant (p├бra) ones, stepping
    over those that are lower (├бvara), thrice seven times did the departed
    (p├бreta) seers bear back death with the track-obstructor.
Notes

Ppp. reads for b apakr─Бmanto duritaс╣Б parehi. In K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 18 and
86. 21, this verse is quoted with vs. 22 ‘for the purpose expressed in
the texts’ (mantroktam); and in 71. 19 and in 86. 22 the second
half-verse is quoted to accompany ’the effacement (lup) of the tracks
to the streams.’ тМКW’s “(lup)” was intended to express his doubt as to
the warrantableness of Bloomfield’s change of lup to yup. Caland
expresses the same doubt, WZKM. viii. 369: cf. his Todtengebr├дuche, p.
120.тМЛ

Griffith

On pathways swept by wind, directed upward, passing beyond the lower, on the higher, Thrice seven times have the Rishis, the Departed, forced Mrityu backward with the fastened fetter.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Come ye, obstructing the track of death, assuming further on a
    longer life-time; sitting in your station, thrust ye [away] death;
    then may we, living, speak to the council.
Notes

The first half-verse is RV. x. 18. 2 a, b, and is found also in TA.
(vi. 10. 2); for our ├й тАЩta, RV. reads y├бd ─Б├нta, TA. y├бd ─Бima
(─Бima unaccented, unless there is a misprint тМКPoona ed. rightly
─Б├нma, p. 444тМЛ); and TA. has pratar─Б╠Бm in b. тМКCf. MGS. ii. i. 13
and p. 153.тМЛ The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 20 and 86. 23 in
connection with doing something to (symbolical) boats; and the second
half-verse in K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 10. Ppp. reads pratiram in b, and j─лv─Бs
in d, thus in the latter p─Бda rectifying the meter. The Anukr. takes
no notice of the irregularities in a and d, perhaps because they
balance each other. тМКAs to vid├бtham, cf. note to vs. 22, and
Bloomfield in JAOS. xix.┬▓ 14.тМЛ

Griffith

Effecting Mrityu’s footstep ye came hither, to further times pro- longing your existence, Seated, drive Mrityu to his proper dwelling: then may we, living, speak to the assembly.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let these women, not widows, well-spoused, touch themselves with
    ointment, with butter; tearless, without disease, with good treasures
    (-r├бtna), let the wives ascend first to the place of union (y├│ni).
Notes

This verse is repeated below, as xviii. 3. 57. It is RV. x. 18. 7, and
found also in TA. (vi. 10. 2). RV. has vi┼Ыantu, and TA. mс╣Ы┼Ыant─Бm,
for our spс╣Ы┼Ыant─Бm in b, and TA. su┼Ы├йvas for sur├бtn─Бs in c;
RV. also combines ana┼Ыr├бvo тАШnam- in c. Ppp. reads saс╣Б vi┼Ыanta in
b; and it adds another corresponding verse for the men: ime v─лrar
avidhav─Бs suj─Бnay─Б nar─Б тАЭ├▒janena sarpiс╣г─Б etc. (d) syon─Бd yoner
adhi talpaс╣Б vс╣Ыheyuс╕е тМКintending ruheyuс╕етМЛ. With our verse, in K─Бu┼Ы. 72.
11, grass shoots dipped in butter are handed to the women; and 72. 12
appears to quote the Ppp. verse (the prat─лka is given as ime j─лv─Б
avidhav─Бс╕е suj─Бmaya) to accompany a similar act to the men.

Griffith

Let these unwidowed dames with goodly husbands adorn them- selves with fragrant balm and unguent, Decked with fair jewels, tearless, sound and healthy, first let the dames go up to where he lieth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I separate (vy-─Б-kс╣Ы) these two by oblation; I shape them apart
    with a spell (br├бhman); I make for the Fathers unwasting svadh─Б╠Б; I
    unite these with a long life-time.
Notes

Ppp. reads for c sudh─Бс╣Б pitс╣Ыbhyo amс╣Ыtam duh─Бn─Б. From V─Бit. 6. 2
the separation would appear to be that of the other two fires when taken
from the householder’s fire; but K─Бu┼Ы. 70. 10 has it repeated while one
looks upon the householder’s and the flesh-eating fires; the latter is
most likely to be its true application. It is also quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 72.
13 with several other verses, from this hymn and elsewhere, as noted
under vs. 24.

Griffith

I with oblation separate both classes, and with my prayer dis- part their several portions. I offer food that wastes not to the Fathers, a nd to these men give life of long duration.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What Agni, O Fathers, hath entered into our hearts, an immortal into
    mortals, that god do I enclose in me; let him not hate us, nor let us
    [hate] him.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b amartyas for amс╣Ыtas, and, in c, mahyaс╣Б taс╣Б
prati gс╣Ыh-. The verse is found also in TS. (v. 7. 9┬╣) and MS. (i. 6.
1); both read, for b, ├бmartyo m├бrty─Бс╣Е ─Бviv├й┼Ыa; for c, d, TS.
has t├бm ─Бtm├бn p├бri gс╣Ыhс╣З─лmahe vay├бm m─Б╠Б s├│ asm─Б╠Бс╣Е avah─Б╠Бya p├бr─Б g─Бt, and
MS. t├бm ─Бtm├бni p├бri gс╣Ыhс╣З─лmas─л тАЩh├б n├йd eс╣г├│ asm─Б╠Бn avah─Б╠Бya par─Б╠Бyat. The
verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 70. 15 for recitation while the hearts are
touched.

Griffith

That Agni, Fathers! who, himself immortal, hath entered and possessed our mortal bosoms, Even him I grasp and hold the God with me, Let him not hate us, may we never hate him.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрдм рдпреЛрдЧреА рдЬрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рд╕реЗ рдЙрд╕ рдЕрд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢реА рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЛ рд╕рдм рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдореЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдореЗрдВ рднреАрддрд░ рд╕рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреН рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рддрдм рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдЙрд╕ рд╕реЗ рдФрд░ рд╡рд╣ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерейрейрее

Translation

reads ├бsti at end of c.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A mortal, going down to mishap, speaks forth repeatedly with greedy
    ones (? gс╣Ы╠Бdhya); whom (pl.) the flesh-eating Agni, from near by,
    after-knowing, follows (? vi-t─Бv).
Notes

The translation is purely mechanical, the sense being wholly obscure.
Nothing corresponding to vit─Б╠Бvati is found anywhere else; the Pet.
Lex. suggests emendation to vidh─Бvati; Ludwig, alternatively, to
vit─Бmyati or vit─Бmati. Yet c, d are repeated below as 52 c,
d (that verse is wanting in Ppp., which, however, has these two p─Бdas
in vs. 50). The much corrupted version of Ppp. gives no help as to the
verse in general: bahu krudh─лс╣г pra vadanty anti tarmato тАШnveti ca:
kravy─Бdam agnir тМКintending kravy─Бd yam ag-?тМЛ anuvidv─Бn vibh─Бvati
(vit─Бvati?).

Griffith

Oft as a greedy beggar speaks the mortal who has brought distress, Those whom Carnivorous Agni close at hand runs after and detects.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The houses are united with seizure (gr─Б╠Бhi) when a woman’s husband
    dies; a knowing priest (brahm├бn) is to be sought, who shall remove the
    flesh-eating one.
Notes

Ppp. reads in b yat str─лy─Бm mriyate. ‘United’ (in a), i.e.
‘caused to be affected.’

Griffith

When a dame’s husband dies the house is tangled in Grahi’s net. A learned Brahman must be sought to drive Carnivorous Agni, forth.

Translation
  1. What evil (ripr├б), pollution we have committed, and what
    ill-doing, from that let the waters cleanse me, and from the crushing
    Agni what.
Notes

The last clause seems a false construction, the true one being something
like the version of Ppp.: agnis saс╣Бkusika┼Ы ca yaс╕е; but Ludwig fills it
out to “and [from that] which [arises] from Agni Saс╣Бkasuka.” тМКAs to
the construction, see Caland as cited under vs. 19.тМЛ тМКAs to saс╣Бkasuka,
cf. note to vs. 11.тМЛ Ppp. further reads duritaс╣Б (for ┼Ыamalam) in
a; and it has ┼Ыundhantu in c тМКcf. note to vi. 115. 3 and the
VS. variant thereтМЛ. The Anukr. understands the verse as 6 + 8: 8 + 8 =
30 syllables; but the pada-mss., less acceptably, mark the p─Бda
division as occurring after cakс╣Ыm├б. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 71.
16 and 86. 19 in company with others, as noted under vs. 13.

Griffith

From any evil we have done, act of impurity or sin, Let waters purge me and from all that comes from Agni Breaker-up.

Whitney
Translation
  1. These fore-knowing ones (f.) have turned hither upward from below by
    roads that the gods go upon; upon the back of the virile (vс╣Ыс╣гabh├б)
    mountain the ancient streams (sar├нt) go about new.
Notes

‘Waters’ (─Б╠Бpas) is doubtless to be supplied with the adjectives in
a, b. Ppp. combines t─Б тАЩdhar─Бd at the beginning, and reads
с╣Ыс╣гabhasya in c. It is doubtless by a blunder (catasras for
tisras) that the Anukr. appears to reckon this regular triс╣гс╣нubh to
the anuс╣гс╣нubhs of the hymn. The verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 3.

Griffith

By pathways travelled by the Gods these waters, well-knowing, from below have mounted upward. High on the summit of the raining mountain the ancient rivers fresh and new are flowing.

  1. O non-flesh-eating Agni, push out the flesh-eating one; bring the
    god-sacrificing one.

other verses, as noted under vs. 1 above. тМКThe first half-verse is
defaced in Ppp.тМЛ

Griffith

Drive off Carnivorous Agni, thou Agni who eatest not the flesh;. carry oblation paid to Gods.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The flesh-eating one entered into this man; he has gone after the
    flesh-eating one; having made two tigers severally, I take him, who is
    other than propitious.
Notes

Ppp. reads pra vive┼Ыa in a, and n─Бn─Б тАЩhaс╣Б in c. The verse is
quoted, with others (see note to vs. 1), in K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 8.

Griffith

The Flesh-eater hath entered him: he hath pursued the Flesh- eater. Making two tigers different-wise, I bear away the ungracious one.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Concealment of the gods, defense (paridh├н) of men (manuс╣гy├а), the
    householder’s fire is set (┼Ыrit├б) between both classes.
Notes

In accordance with the Anukr., the mss. interpose no stroke of
interpunction in this verse, which plainly is not metrical, though the
last 8 syllables read like an anuс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. It is quoted, with others
(see note to vs. 24), in K─Бu┼Ы. 72. 13. Ppp. reads ubhay─Бd in c.
тМКThe medial avas─Бna is lacking in SPP. and should be deleted from the
Berlin ed.тМЛ

Griffith

He who holds Gods within himself, the rampart and defence of men, Agni, the sacred household fire, hath come and stands between them both.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Lengthen thou out, O Agni, the life-time of the living; let them who
    are dead go unto the world of the Fathers; do thou, a good householder’s
    fire, burning away the niggard, assign to this man an ever better dawn.
Notes

Ppp. reads, for a, j─лv─Бn─Бm agneс╣г pratar d─лrgham ─Бyuс╣г, and, in c,
d, ar─Бt─лr uс╣г─Бm-uс╣г─Бс╣Б ┼Ыrayaс╣Б ┼Ыrayasi dadhat. K─Бu┼Ы. and V─Бit. quote as
prat─лka only the beginning of c; this looks rather as if they
made one verse of our 45 c, d and 46. In K─Бu┼Ы. (71. 2) it
accompanies setting down fuel on the householder’s fire; in V─Бit. (4. 8)
it is used with one of the offerings of the sacrificer’s wife. It (11 +
13: 11 + 11 = 46) is very ill defined as simply a jagat─л.

Griffith

Prolong the lives of those who live, O Agni, Let the dead go unto world of Fathers. As goodly household fire burn up Arati; give this man dawn brighter than all the mornings.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Lay ye hold after the draft-ox [as] float (plav├б); he shall
    carry you out of difficulty [and] reproach; mount this boat of
    Savitar; may we cross over misery by the six wide [directions].
Notes

This and the remaining verses of the hymn are given by Ppp. in the order
49-51, 54, 53, 55, 48 (52 being wanting). тМКCf. MGS. ii. i. 14 and p.
146.тМЛ In K─Бu┼Ы. 72.8, this verse and the next are used (next after vss.
28, 47) in laying hold on a couch (talpa); the third p─Бda in 71. 23
and 86. 26, in causing some one to embark on a (symbolical) boat
containing gold and barley. There is no good reason for calling the
verse bhurij.

Griffith

Seize with firm hold the Ox who boundeth forward: he will uplift you from disgrace and trouble. Enter this ship of Savitar; let us flee from poverty over all the six expenses.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Day-and-night thou goest after, bearing, standing comfortable
    (kс╣гemy├б), prolonging [life], having good heroes; bearing, O couch,

in a. The use by K─Бu┼Ы. was noticed under the preceding verse.

Griffith

Thou followest the day and night, supporting, standing, at peace, promoting, rich in heroes. Long bearing undiseased and happy sleepers, be ours, O Bed, with smell of man about thee,

Whitney
Translation
  1. They fall under the wrath of the gods, they live always evilly,
    after whom the flesh-eating fire, from near by, like a horse, scatters
    reeds.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a deveс╣гu, and this is the usual and regular
construction with ─Б-vra┼Ыc. Further, for d it has our 38 d and
52 d. The Anukr. gives iva two syllables in d. Our Bp. reads
antik─Б╠Бn (instead of -k─Б╠Бt here and in 38 c and 52 c. тМКOne
could easily scan d as an anuс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda, ├б┼Ыvev─Бnv├бpate naс╕Н├бm
(Gram. ┬з233 a), if it were worth scanning.тМЛ

Griffith

They sever from the Gods, they live in sin and misery evermore, Those whom from very near at hand Carnivorous Agni casteth down as a horse tramples down the reeds.

The faithless, who from lust of wealth abide with him who feeds on flesh, For ever set upon the fire an alien caldron, not their own.

Whitney
Translation
  1. A black ewe [is] of cattle [thy] portion; lead, too, they call
    thy gold (? candr├б), O flesh-eating one; ground beans тМКareтМЛ thy
    portion [as] oblation; seek (sac) thou the thicket of the
    forest-spirit (araс╣Зy─Бn─л╠Б).
Notes

Ppp. reads (better) uta for api in b. The verse is quoted in
K─Бu┼Ы. 71. 6 (with vss. 4 and 7: see note to vs. 4), and again in 71. 14,
in connection with setting down the light (d─лpa).

Griffith

Among tame beasts the black ewe is thy portion, and the bright lead is thine, they say, Flesh-eater! Mashed beans have been assigned thee for oblation go seek the dark wood and the wildernesses.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Having made offering of withered (? j├бrat) cane (iс╣г─л╠Бk─Б), of
    tilp├н├▒ja, of d├бс╣Зс╕Нana, of reeds; having made fuel of this, Indra
    removed Yama’s fire.
Notes

Various kinds of red or cane are doubtless named in a, b. Jarant
is lit. ‘aged.’ Ppp. reads in c t─Бn indre тАЩdhmaс╣Б. The Anukr. does
not note c as defective; we may resolve either ├нndс╣Ы-a or kс╣Ыtu-─Б╠Б.
The verse is quoted (with vss. 1, 11, 55: see note to vs. 1) in K─Бu┼Ы.
71. 5, to accompany the feeding of the flesh-eating fire.

Griffith

I sought the rustling sugar-cane, white Seasamum, and cane and reed. I made this Indra’s fuel, and the Fire of Yama I removed.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Having sent in opposition an opposing (praty├б├▒c) song (ark├б), I,
    foreknowing, have entered abroad on the road; I have directed away the
    lifebreaths of them yonder; these here I unite with long life-time.
Notes

The first half-verse is difficult and doubtful. The use made of the
verse by K─Бu┼Ы. gives no help; it is quoted in 71. 5 as noted above,
under vs. 54; and in 72. 13 with several other verses, as noted under
vs. 24. Ppp. reads ─Бcak─Бra at end of b. тМКW. has overlooked the
h├н and the accent of the two perfects: perhaps, ‘since I have entered
[and] have directed…, [accordingly] I unite’ etc. Henry, p. 238,
inserts another h├н after am─л╠Бс╣г─Бm.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the second anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 55 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says “naс╕Нas” tu pa├▒con─Б.тМЛ

Griffith

Against the sinking western Sun I set them; each sundered path, knowing my way, I entered. I have warned off the ghosts of the Departed: to these I give the boon of long existence.
